href="#cite_note-lufthansagroup_annual_report-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://lufthansa.com">lufthansa<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Deutsche Lufthansa <a href="/wiki/Aktiengesellschaft" title="Aktiengesellschaft">AG</a></b> (<small>German pronunciation:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[\xcb\x8cd\xc9\x94\xca\x8ft\xca\x83\xc9\x99 \xcb\x88l\xca\x8afthanza\xcb\x90]</a></span>), commonly known as <b>Lufthansa</b>, is the largest <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airline</a> which, when combined with its subsidiaries, is the second-<a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_airlines_in_Europe" title="List of largest airlines in Europe">largest airline in Europe</a> in terms of passengers carried.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The name of the former <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a><sup id="cite_ref-Lufthansa_privatization_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lufthansa_privatization-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> is derived from the German word <i>Luft</i> meaning "air" and <i>Hansa</i> for the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a>. Lufthansa is one of the five founding members of <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a>, the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Airline_alliance" title="Airline alliance">airline alliance</a>, formed in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The company slogan is \'Say yes to the world.\'<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Besides its own services, and owning subsidiary passenger airlines <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swiss_International_Air_Lines" title="Swiss International Air Lines">Swiss International Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> (referred to in English by Lufthansa as its <i>Passenger Airline Group</i>), Deutsche Lufthansa AG owns several aviation-related companies, such as <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Technik" title="Lufthansa Technik">Lufthansa Technik</a> and <a href="/wiki/LSG_Sky_Chefs" class="mw-redirect" title="LSG Sky Chefs">LSG Sky Chefs</a>, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Group" title="Lufthansa Group">Lufthansa Group</a>. In total, the group has over 700 aircraft, making it one of the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_largest_airlines#By_fleet_size" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s largest airlines">largest airline fleets in the world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LufthansaSubsidiaryFleet_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LufthansaSubsidiaryFleet-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lufthansa\'s <a href="/wiki/Registered_office" title="Registered office">registered office</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corporate_headquarters" title="Corporate headquarters">corporate headquarters</a> are in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>. The main operations base, called Lufthansa Aviation Center, is at Lufthansa\'s primary hub at <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and its secondary hub is at <a href="/wiki/Munich_Airport" title="Munich Airport">Munich Airport</a> where a secondary <i>Flight Operations Centre</i> is maintained.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span incidents</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Fatal"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Fatal</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Non-fatal"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Non-fatal</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Hijackings"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Hijackings</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Criticism"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Criticism</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Employment_relations"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Employment relations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a href="#Germanwings_crisis_management"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Germanwings crisis tocsection-43"><a href="#Deportation_flights"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Deportation flights</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-44"><a href="#Treatment_of_World_War_II-era_past"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Treatment of World War II-era past</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-47"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-48"><a href="#Citations"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-50"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="1950s:_Post-war_.28re-.29formation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1950s:_Post-war_(re-)formation">1950s: Post-war (re-)formation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1950s: Post-war (re-)formation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb  tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px;font-size:88%">\n<table class="wikitable" style="display:table;background: #fefefe;width:100%;margin-top:0;text-align:center">\n<caption style="display:table-caption">\nRevenue Passenger-Kilometers, scheduled flights only, in millions\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>Traffic\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1955\n</td>\n<td>78\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1960\n</td>\n<td>1,284\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1965\n</td>\n<td>3,785\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1969\n</td>\n<td>6,922\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1971\n</td>\n<td>8,610\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1975\n</td>\n<td>13,634\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1980\n</td>\n<td>21,056\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1989\n</td>\n<td>36,133\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1995\n</td>\n<td>61,602\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2000\n</td>\n<td>94,170\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="font-size:8pt;text-align:left">Source: ICAO Digest of Statistics for 1955, IATA World Air Transport Statistics 1960-2000</div>\n</div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Convair_340-61_D-ACAD_Lufthansa_LAP_03.09.55_edited-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Convair_340-61_D-ACAD_Lufthansa_LAP_03.09.55_edited-2.jpg/220px-Convair_340-61_D-ACAD_Lufthansa_LAP_03.09.55_edited-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Convair_340-61_D-ACAD_Lufthansa_LAP_03.09.55_edited-2.jpg/330px-Convair_340-61_D-ACAD_Lufthansa_LAP_03.09.55_edited-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Convair_340-61_D-ACAD_Lufthansa_LAP_03.09.55_edited-2.jpg/440px-Convair_340-61_D-ACAD_Lufthansa_LAP_03.09.55_edited-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1085" data-file-height="667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Convair_340-61_D-ACAD_Lufthansa_LAP_03.09.55_edited-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lufthansa\'s first aircraft, a <a href="/wiki/Convair_240" class="mw-redirect" title="Convair 240">Convair 340</a> <i>(type pictured)</i>, was delivered in August 1954.</div></div></div>\n<p>Lufthansa traces its history to 1926 when <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Luft_Hansa" title="Deutsche Luft Hansa">Deutsche Luft Hansa</a> <a href="/wiki/Aktiengesellschaft" title="Aktiengesellschaft">A.G.</a> (styled as <i>Deutsche Lufthansa</i> from 1933 onwards) was formed in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DLHhistory_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DLHhistory-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> DLH, as it was known, was Germany\'s <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> until 1945 when all services were terminated following the defeat of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>; it has since been demonstrated that Deutsche Luft Hansa relied on the use of forced labor and housed forced laborers on the site of Tempelhof airport.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In an effort to create a new national airline, a company called <b>Aktiengesellschaft f\xc3\xbcr Luftverkehrsbedarf</b> (<b>Luftag</b>),<sup id="cite_ref-fi54_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fi54-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> was founded in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> on 6 January 1953, with many of its staff having worked for the pre-war Lufthansa; this included Kurt Weigelt, a Nazi convicted of war crimes who served on the board on the new Lufthansa, and Kurt Knipfer, a member of the Nazi party from 1929 who led Luft Hansa from 1933 to 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><br />\n<a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> had not yet been granted sovereignty over its airspace, so it was not known when the new airline could become operational. Nevertheless, in 1953 Luftag placed orders for four <a href="/wiki/Convair_CV-340" class="mw-redirect" title="Convair CV-340">Convair CV-340s</a> and four <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_L-1049_Super_Constellation" title="Lockheed L-1049 Super Constellation">Lockheed L-1049 Super Constellations</a> and set up a maintenance base at <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Airport" title="Hamburg Airport">Hamburg Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fi54_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fi54-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lex_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lex-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> On 6 August 1954, Luftag acquired the name and logo of the liquidated Deutsche Lufthansa for <a href="/wiki/German_Mark" class="mw-redirect" title="German Mark">DM</a> 30,000 (equivalent to \xe2\x82\xac38000 today),<sup id="cite_ref-lex_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lex-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> thus continuing the tradition of a German flag carrier of that name.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lockheed_L-1049G_D-ALAP_LH_RWY_06.05.56_edited-4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Lockheed_L-1049G_D-ALAP_LH_RWY_06.05.56_edited-4.jpg/220px-Lockheed_L-1049G_D-ALAP_LH_RWY_06.05.56_edited-4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Lockheed_L-1049G_D-ALAP_LH_RWY_06.05.56_edited-4.jpg/330px-Lockheed_L-1049G_D-ALAP_LH_RWY_06.05.56_edited-4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Lockheed_L-1049G_D-ALAP_LH_RWY_06.05.56_edited-4.jpg/440px-Lockheed_L-1049G_D-ALAP_LH_RWY_06.05.56_edited-4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1025" data-file-height="668" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lockheed_L-1049G_D-ALAP_LH_RWY_06.05.56_edited-4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lufthansa Lockheed L-1049G Super Constellation operating a transatlantic scheduled service from Hamburg to Montreal and Chicago in May 1956</div></div></div>\n<p>On 1 April 1955 Lufthansa won approval to start scheduled domestic flights,<sup id="cite_ref-lex_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lex-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> linking <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fg15041955_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg15041955-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> International flights started on 15 May 1955, to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-fg15041955_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg15041955-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sp55_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sp55-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Super_Constellation" class="mw-redirect" title="Super Constellation">Super Constellation</a> flights to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> from 1 June of that year,<sup id="cite_ref-fg15041955_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg15041955-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and across the South Atlantic from August 1956. In August 1958 fifteen Lufthansa 1049Gs and 1649s left Germany each week to Canada and the United States, three 1049Gs a week flew to South America, three flew to Tehran and one to Baghdad. In parallel, the airline also initiated a marketing campaign to sell itself and West Germany. The challenges involved encouraging travelers to consider visiting the country in the wake of World War II, as well as offering services to other nations via the Frankfurt airport hub. More specifically, Lufthansa\'s efforts shaped and reflected the development of a modern form of consumerism and advertising through the sale of air travel. By 1963, the airline, initially limited in its public relations efforts, had become a major purveyor of West Germany\'s image abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Soviet_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Soviet Zone">special status</a> of Berlin meant that Lufthansa was not allowed to fly to either part of <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> until <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> in 1990. Originally thought to be only a temporary matter (and with intentions to move the airline\'s headquarters and main base there once the political situation changed),<sup id="cite_ref-fi54_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fi54-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Germany_(1945%E2%80%9390)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Germany (1945\xe2\x80\x9390)">Division of Germany</a> turned out to be longer than expected, which gradually led to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a> becoming Lufthansa\'s primary <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> tried to establish <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Lufthansa_(East_Germany)" title="Deutsche Lufthansa (East Germany)">its airline</a> in 1955 using the <i>Lufthansa</i> name, but this resulted in a legal dispute with <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>, where Lufthansa was operating. East Germany instead established <a href="/wiki/Interflug" title="Interflug">Interflug</a> as its national airline in 1963, which coincided with the East German Lufthansa being shut down.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960s:_Introduction_of_jetliners">1960s: Introduction of jetliners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1960s: Introduction of jetliners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_707-330B,_Lufthansa_AN2025731.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Boeing_707-330B%2C_Lufthansa_AN2025731.jpg/220px-Boeing_707-330B%2C_Lufthansa_AN2025731.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Boeing_707-330B%2C_Lufthansa_AN2025731.jpg/330px-Boeing_707-330B%2C_Lufthansa_AN2025731.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Boeing_707-330B%2C_Lufthansa_AN2025731.jpg/440px-Boeing_707-330B%2C_Lufthansa_AN2025731.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="708" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_707-330B,_Lufthansa_AN2025731.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 1960, Lufthansa joined the <a href="/wiki/Jet_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Jet age">jet age</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">Boeing 707</a>. The image shows a 707 at <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Airport" title="Hamburg Airport">Hamburg Airport</a> in 1984, shortly before the type was retired.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lufthansa_Boeing_727-30C_Fitzgerald.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Lufthansa_Boeing_727-30C_Fitzgerald.jpg/220px-Lufthansa_Boeing_727-30C_Fitzgerald.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Lufthansa_Boeing_727-30C_Fitzgerald.jpg/330px-Lufthansa_Boeing_727-30C_Fitzgerald.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Lufthansa_Boeing_727-30C_Fitzgerald.jpg/440px-Lufthansa_Boeing_727-30C_Fitzgerald.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lufthansa_Boeing_727-30C_Fitzgerald.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Lufthansa <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing 727-100</a> approaching <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a> in 1978.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1958 Lufthansa ordered four <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">Boeing 707s</a> and started jet flights from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> to New York City in March 1960. <a href="/wiki/Boeing_720" title="Boeing 720">Boeing 720</a>Bs were later bought to back up the 707 fleets. In February 1961 Far East routes were extended beyond <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, Thailand, to Hong Kong and Tokyo. <a href="/wiki/Lagos" title="Lagos">Lagos</a>, Nigeria, and <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>, South Africa were added in 1962.\n</p><p>Lufthansa introduced the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing 727</a> in 1964 and that May began the <a href="/wiki/Polar_route" title="Polar route">Polar route</a> from Frankfurt to Tokyo via Anchorage. In February 1965 the company ordered twenty-one <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737s</a> that went into service in 1968. Lufthansa was the first customer for the Boeing 737 and was one of four buyers of the 737-100s (the others were <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia-Singapore_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Malaysia-Singapore Airlines">Malaysia-Singapore Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Avianca" title="Avianca">Avianca</a> \xe2\x80\x93 while the NASA airframe was the first built, it was the last delivered and originally intended for delivery to Lufthansa). Lufthansa was the first foreign launch customer for a Boeing airliner.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1970s.E2.80.931980s:_The_wide-body_era"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s\xe2\x80\x931980s:_The_wide-body_era">1970s\xe2\x80\x931980s: The wide-body era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1970s\xe2\x80\x931980s: The wide-body era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Wide-body" class="mw-redirect" title="Wide-body">wide-body</a> era for Lufthansa started with a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> flight on 26 April 1970. It was followed by the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10">DC-10-30</a> on 12 November 1973, and the first <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A300" title="Airbus A300">Airbus A300</a> in 1976. In 1979 Lufthansa and <a href="/wiki/Swissair" title="Swissair">Swissair</a> became launch customers for the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A310" title="Airbus A310">Airbus A310</a> with an order for twenty-five aircraft.\n</p><p>The company\'s fleet modernization programme for the 1990s began on 29 June 1985, with an order for fifteen <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320s</a> and seven <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A300" title="Airbus A300">Airbus A300-600s</a>. Ten <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Classic" title="Boeing 737 Classic">Boeing 737-300s</a> were ordered a few days later. All were delivered between 1987 and 1992. Lufthansa also bought <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340" title="Airbus A340">Airbus A340</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> aircraft.\n</p><p>In 1987 Lufthansa, together with <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iberia_(airline)" title="Iberia (airline)">Iberia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a>, founded <a href="/wiki/Amadeus_IT_Group" title="Amadeus IT Group">Amadeus</a>, an IT company (also known as a <a href="/wiki/Computer_reservations_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer reservations system">GDS</a>) that would enable travel agencies to sell the founders and other airlines\' products from a single system.\n</p><p>Lufthansa adopted a new corporate identity in 1988. The fleet was given a new livery, while cabins, city offices, and airport lounges were redesigned.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1990s.E2.80.932000s:_Further_expansion"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s\xe2\x80\x932000s:_Further_expansion">1990s\xe2\x80\x932000s: Further expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1990s\xe2\x80\x932000s: Further expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lufthansa_737-130_D-ABED.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Lufthansa_737-130_D-ABED.jpg/220px-Lufthansa_737-130_D-ABED.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Lufthansa_737-130_D-ABED.jpg/330px-Lufthansa_737-130_D-ABED.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Lufthansa_737-130_D-ABED.jpg/440px-Lufthansa_737-130_D-ABED.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lufthansa_737-130_D-ABED.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lufthansa was the launch customer of the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a>, the best-selling jet airliner for long time until replaced by <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320">Airbus A320</a> in late 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight15nov2019_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight15nov2019-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The image shows an original 737-100 at <a href="/wiki/Hannover_Airport" title="Hannover Airport">Hannover Airport</a> in 1968.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A300B4-605R,_Lufthansa_AN0481981.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Airbus_A300B4-605R%2C_Lufthansa_AN0481981.jpg/220px-Airbus_A300B4-605R%2C_Lufthansa_AN0481981.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Airbus_A300B4-605R%2C_Lufthansa_AN0481981.jpg/330px-Airbus_A300B4-605R%2C_Lufthansa_AN0481981.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Airbus_A300B4-605R%2C_Lufthansa_AN0481981.jpg/440px-Airbus_A300B4-605R%2C_Lufthansa_AN0481981.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="775" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A300B4-605R,_Lufthansa_AN0481981.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lufthansa operated the high-capacity <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A300" title="Airbus A300">Airbus A300-600</a> on domestic and European routes until 2009. The image shows an aircraft of that type on <a href="/wiki/Final_approach_(aviation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Final approach (aviation)">final approach</a> at Frankfurt Airport in 2003.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 28 October 1990, 25 days after <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">reunification</a>, Berlin became a Lufthansa destination again. On 18 May 1997, Lufthansa, <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thai_Airways_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Thai Airways International">Thai Airways International</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> formed <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a>, the world\'s first multilateral <a href="/wiki/Airline_alliance" title="Airline alliance">airline alliance</a>.\n</p><p>In 1999, Lufthansa participated in the German Business Foundation initiative addressing class action lawsuits against German companies for World War II-era misdeeds, including the use of forced labor, by reportedly paying 10s of millions German marks.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The same year, Lufthansa commissioned the scholar Lutz Budrass to investigate the use of forced labor by its predecessor company, Deutsche Luft Hansa, during World War II; it declined to publish Dr. Budrass\'s resulting study for more than a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2000, <a href="/wiki/Air_One" title="Air One">Air One</a> became a Lufthansa partner airline and nearly all Air One flights were code-shared with Lufthansa until <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a> purchased Air One. Lufthansa has a good track record for posting profits, even in 2001, after <a href="/wiki/September_11,_2001_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="September 11, 2001 attacks">9/11</a>, the airline suffered a significant loss in profits but still managed to stay \'in the black\'. While many other airlines announced layoffs (typically 20% of their workforce), Lufthansa retained its current workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 December 2001, Lufthansa announced an order for 15 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> superjumbos with 10 more options, which was confirmed on 20 December. The A380 fleet would be used for long-haul flights from Frankfurt exclusively.\n</p><p>In June 2003, Lufthansa opened Terminal 2 at <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Strau%C3%9F_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Franz Josef Strau\xc3\x9f Airport">Franz Josef Strau\xc3\x9f Airport</a> to relieve its main hub, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, which was suffering from capacity constraints. It is one of the first <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminals</a> in Europe partially owned by an airline.\n</p><p>On 17 May 2004, Lufthansa became the launch customer for the <a href="/wiki/Connexion_by_Boeing" title="Connexion by Boeing">Connexion by Boeing</a> in-flight online connectivity service.\n</p><p>In autumn 2003, the implementation of a new sales strategy initiated by then-incumbent <a href="/wiki/Executive_Vice_President" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive Vice President">Executive Vice President</a> Thierry Antinori to make the company fit for the digital era led to the abolition of commission payments for <a href="/wiki/Travel_agencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Travel agencies">travel agencies</a> and led to a revolution in the German travel business with many travel agencies disappearing from the market on the one hand, and the rise of new <a href="/wiki/Digital_data" title="Digital data">digital</a> distribution platforms on the other hand.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 22 March 2005, <a href="/wiki/Swiss_International_Air_Lines" title="Swiss International Air Lines">Swiss International Air Lines</a> was purchased by Lufthansa\'s holding company. The acquisition included the provision that the majority shareholders (the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Switzerland" title="Politics of Switzerland">Swiss government</a> and large Swiss companies) be offered payment if Lufthansa\'s share price outperforms an airline index during the years following the merger. The two companies will continue to be run separately.\n</p><p>On 6 December 2006, Lufthansa placed an order for 20 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-8" title="Boeing 747-8">Boeing 747-8s</a>, becoming the launch customer of the passenger model. The airline is also the second European airline to operate the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> (after <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>). The first A380 was delivered on 19 May 2010, while the first 747-8 entered service in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2008, Lufthansa Group announced its intent to purchase a stake in <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a> (SN). In June 2009, the EU Commission granted regulatory approval and Lufthansa acquired 45% of SN.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In September 2016, Lufthansa announced it would purchase the remainder of Brussels Airlines for \xe2\x82\xac2.6 million <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euros</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The transaction was completed in early January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The decision was partially taken after the <a href="/wiki/2016_Brussels_bombings" title="2016 Brussels bombings">Brussels airport bombings of March 2016</a>, which caused SN to lose almost \xe2\x82\xac5 million per day until 3 April.\n</p><p>In September 2009, Lufthansa purchased Austrian Airlines with the approval of the European Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 June 2010, Airbus A380 service between Frankfurt and Tokyo (<a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">Narita</a>) started.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s:_Belt-tightening">2010s: Belt-tightening</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2010s: Belt-tightening">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lufthansa_Airbus_A380_and_Boeing_747_(16431502906).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Lufthansa_Airbus_A380_and_Boeing_747_%2816431502906%29.jpg/220px-Lufthansa_Airbus_A380_and_Boeing_747_%2816431502906%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Lufthansa_Airbus_A380_and_Boeing_747_%2816431502906%29.jpg/330px-Lufthansa_Airbus_A380_and_Boeing_747_%2816431502906%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Lufthansa_Airbus_A380_and_Boeing_747_%2816431502906%29.jpg/440px-Lufthansa_Airbus_A380_and_Boeing_747_%2816431502906%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2469" data-file-height="1389" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lufthansa_Airbus_A380_and_Boeing_747_(16431502906).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-8I" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-8I">Boeing 747-8I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380-800</a> of Lufthansa at <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>. The A380 and 747-8, together with the recently introduced <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350 XWB">Airbus A350 XWB</a>, form the backbone for Lufthansa\'s long-haul routes.</div></div></div>\n<p>After a loss of 381 million euros in the first quarter of 2010 and another 13 million loss in the year 2011 due to the economic recession and restructuring costs, Deutsche Lufthansa AG cut 3,500 administrative positions or around 20 percent of the clerical total of 16,800.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, Lufthansa announced a restructuring program called SCORE to improve its operating profit. As a part of the restructuring plan, the company started to transfer all short-haul flights outside its hubs in Frankfurt, Munich, and D\xc3\xbcsseldorf to the company\'s re-branded <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Germanwings" title="Germanwings">Germanwings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2013, Lufthansa Group announced its biggest order, for 59 wide-body aircraft valued more than 14 billion euros at list prices. Earlier in the same year, Lufthansa placed an order for 100 next-generation narrow-body aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The group has had a long-standing dispute with the Vereinigung Cockpit union which has demanded a scheme in which pilots can retire at the age of 55, and 60% of their pay be retained, which Lufthansa insists is no longer affordable. Lufthansa pilots were joined by pilots from the group\'s budget carrier Germanwings to stage a nationwide strike in support of their demands in April 2014 which lasted three days. The pilots staged a six-hour strike at the end of the summer holidays in September 2014, which caused the cancellation of 200 Lufthansa flights and 100 Germanwings flights.<sup id="cite_ref-LufthansaStrike_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LufthansaStrike-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2014, Lufthansa signed an outsourcing deal worth $1.25 billion with <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> that will see the US company take over the airline\'s IT infrastructure services division and staff.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2015, Lufthansa announced plans to close its small long-haul base at <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport</a> for economic reasons by October 2015. At the time, the base consisted of two <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-300">Airbus A340-300s</a> rotating between <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>. As a result, service to Chicago from D\xc3\xbcsseldorf was first made seasonal, suspended for the winter 2015 season, and then canceled altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Service to Newark, however, has been maintained. From the winter 2015 schedule through the end of the winter 2016 schedule, D\xc3\xbcsseldorf was served by aircraft which also flew the Munich-Newark route. The D\xc3\xbcsseldorf-Newark route ended on 30 November 2018, which was operated with an Airbus A330-300 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Their base was officially closed in March 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-rp-online_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rp-online-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nrz.de_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrz.de-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lufthansa_-_Airbus_A321neo_in_Reykjavik_(Quintin_Soloviev).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Lufthansa_-_Airbus_A321neo_in_Reykjavik_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg/220px-Lufthansa_-_Airbus_A321neo_in_Reykjavik_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Lufthansa_-_Airbus_A321neo_in_Reykjavik_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg/330px-Lufthansa_-_Airbus_A321neo_in_Reykjavik_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Lufthansa_-_Airbus_A321neo_in_Reykjavik_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg/440px-Lufthansa_-_Airbus_A321neo_in_Reykjavik_%28Quintin_Soloviev%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7848" data-file-height="5234" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lufthansa_-_Airbus_A321neo_in_Reykjavik_(Quintin_Soloviev).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Lufthansa A321neo in Reykjavik</div></div></div>\n<p>On 22 March 2016, Lufthansa ended <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-500" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-500">Boeing 737-500</a> operations.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The airline\'s last Boeing 737 (a 737-300) was retired on 29 October 2016, after a flight from <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> to Frankfurt. Lufthansa operated the 737 in several variants for almost 50 years, the first aircraft having been delivered on 27 December 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-737retirement_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-737retirement-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 4 December 2017, Lufthansa became the first European airline to receive the <a href="/wiki/Skytrax" title="Skytrax">Skytrax</a> 5 star certification.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> As stated by Skytrax, a key factor in the positive rating was the announcement of a new Business Class cabin and seating that was expected to be introduced in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> While this makes Lufthansa the 10th airline to be holding this award, in reality the 5th star was given to a product that was supposed to be introduced two years after the evaluation.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In celebration, Lufthansa painted an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-8" title="Boeing 747-8">Boeing 747-8</a> in the "5 Starhansa" livery.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2018, Lufthansa and other airlines like <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> accepted a request from Beijing to list Taiwan as part of China.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2019 Lufthansa ordered 20 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787-9" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787-9">Boeing 787-9</a> and an additional 20 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350-900" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350-900">Airbus A350-900</a> for its own and the group\'s fleet replacement and expansion. Also, the airline announced it would sell six <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A380-800">A380 aircraft</a> back to Airbus, beginning in 2022.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flugzeuge.Lufthansa.P1056230.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Flugzeuge.Lufthansa.P1056230.jpg/220px-Flugzeuge.Lufthansa.P1056230.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Flugzeuge.Lufthansa.P1056230.jpg/330px-Flugzeuge.Lufthansa.P1056230.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Flugzeuge.Lufthansa.P1056230.jpg/440px-Flugzeuge.Lufthansa.P1056230.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flugzeuge.Lufthansa.P1056230.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>15 aircraft of Lufthansa that are parked at <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport" title="Berlin Brandenburg Airport">Berlin Brandenburg Airport</a> on 21 March 2020 due to the cancellation of 95 percent of all flights of the airline on 19 March 2020</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2020s:_COVID-19_pandemic_and_recovery">2020s: COVID-19 pandemic and recovery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2020s: COVID-19 pandemic and recovery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 19 March 2020 Lufthansa cancelled 95 percent of all flights due to a <a href="/wiki/Travel_restrictions_related_to_the_COVID-19_pandemic" title="Travel restrictions related to the COVID-19 pandemic">travel ban</a> because of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Consequently, the airline incurred losses of 1 million euros per hour by April 2020. While Lufthansa reduced its costs throughout 2020, continuing health risks and travel restrictions still caused hourly losses of approximately 500,000 euros on average at the beginning of 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>  \n</p><p>On 14 May, Lufthansa\'s Hans DeHaan said the airline would resume flights between Toronto and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> as of 3 June. Flights were banned on all <a href="/wiki/International_non-essential_travel" title="International non-essential travel">international non-essential travel</a> between Canada and the European Union. Prior to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, Lufthansa operated 64 weekly flights between the two countries. The airline\'s recovery plans involve high-density cargo to replace paying customers. The <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Group" title="Lufthansa Group">Lufthansa Group</a> airlines now require all passengers to wear a mask while aboard.<sup id="cite_ref-cbcluft_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbcluft-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 26 June, Deutsche Lufthansa AG shareholders voted in favour of accepting the capital measures and the participation of the Economic Stabilisation Fund (WSF) of the Federal Republic of Germany in Deutsche Lufthansa AG.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In total, Lufthansa received about 9 billion euros in government assistance that summer.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2021, Lufthansa CEO Spohr announced that the entire currently stored <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-600" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-600">Airbus A340-600</a> fleet will be retired with immediate effect and not return to service anymore.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lufthansa was a <a href="/wiki/State-owned_enterprise" title="State-owned enterprise">state-owned enterprise</a> (and <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a>) until 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-privatization_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-privatization-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Deutsche Lufthansa AG shares have been publicly traded on all German stock exchanges since 1966. In addition to floor trading, it is also traded electronically using the <a href="/wiki/Xetra_(trading_system)" title="Xetra (trading system)">Xetra system</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/DAX" title="DAX">DAX</a> index share and is listed in the German Stock Exchange\'s Prime Standard.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> At the end of 2019, the shareholders\xe2\x80\x99 register showed that German investors held 67.3% of the shares (previous year: 72.1%). The second-largest group, with 10.4%, was shareholders from Luxembourg. Investors from the US accounted for 8.1%, followed by Ireland and the United Kingdom, each with 3.6%. This ensures compliance with the provisions of the German Aviation Compliance Documentation Act (LuftNaSiG). As of the reporting date, 58% of the shares were held by institutional investors (previous year: 53%), and 42% were held by private individuals (previous year: 47%). Lansdowne Partners International Ltd. and BlackRock, Inc. were the largest shareholders in the Lufthansa Group at year-end, with 4.9% and 3.1% respectively. All the transactions requiring disclosure and published during the financial year 2019, as well as the quarterly updates on the shareholder structure, are available online. During the 2020 COVID crisis <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Hermann_Thiele" title="Heinz Hermann Thiele">Heinz Hermann Thiele</a> increased his stake to more than 12%; he died a few months later. The <a href="/wiki/Free_float" class="mw-redirect" title="Free float">free float</a> for Lufthansa shares was 67% in 2020, as per the definition of the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_B%C3%B6rse" title="Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse">Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse</a>.\n</p><p><b>German Government Bail-out</b>\n</p><p>The German government offered a \xe2\x82\xac9 billion bailout to support the airline through COVID-19 induced economic issues. With this bailout, the government\'s stake in the airline increased to 20%, and also grant it board seats, while diluting existing shareholder stakes.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The shareholders of the company approved the bailout on Thursday, June 26, offering the airline a fresh lease of life.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_trends">Business trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Business trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Key business and operating results of Lufthansa Group for recent years are shown below (as at year ending 31 December):\n</p>\n<table id="cite_ref-Lufthansa_Group:_Annual_Reports_63-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lufthansa_Group:_Annual_Reports-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-Lufthansa_Group:_Annual_Report_2016_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lufthansa_Group:_Annual_Report_2016-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-Lufthansa_Group:_Annual_Reports_63-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lufthansa_Group:_Annual_Reports-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-Lufthansa_Group:_Annual_Reports_63-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lufthansa_Group:_Annual_Reports-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-Lufthansa_Group:_Annual_Reports_63-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lufthansa_Group:_Annual_Reports-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters">Headquarters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Headquarters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LH-HQ,_K%C3%B6ln-Deutz,_Front_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/LH-HQ%2C_K%C3%B6ln-Deutz%2C_Front_3.jpg/220px-LH-HQ%2C_K%C3%B6ln-Deutz%2C_Front_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/LH-HQ%2C_K%C3%B6ln-Deutz%2C_Front_3.jpg/330px-LH-HQ%2C_K%C3%B6ln-Deutz%2C_Front_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/LH-HQ%2C_K%C3%B6ln-Deutz%2C_Front_3.jpg/440px-LH-HQ%2C_K%C3%B6ln-Deutz%2C_Front_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LH-HQ,_K%C3%B6ln-Deutz,_Front_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lufthansa\'s headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Deutz,_Cologne" title="Deutz, Cologne">Deutz, Cologne</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Lufthansa\'s corporate headquarters are in <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>. In 1971, Lawrence Fellows of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> described the then-new headquarters building that Lufthansa occupied in Cologne as "gleaming".<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> In 1986, terrorists bombed the building.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> No one was injured.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, builders laid the first stone of the new Lufthansa headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Deutz,_Cologne" title="Deutz, Cologne">Deutz, Cologne</a>. By the end of 2007, Lufthansa planned to move 800 employees, including the company\'s finance department, to the new building.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> However, in early 2013 Lufthansa revealed plans to relocate its head office from Cologne to Frankfurt by 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several Lufthansa departments are not at the headquarters; instead they are in the Lufthansa Aviation Center at <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>. These departments include Corporate Communications,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Investor Relations,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and Media Relations.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airline_subsidiaries">Airline subsidiaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In addition to its main passenger operation, Lufthansa has several airline subsidiaries, including:<sup id="cite_ref-2012_report_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012_report-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>Wholly owned by Lufthansa</dt></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Regional" title="Lufthansa Regional">Lufthansa Regional</a> &#8211; regional feeder airline\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_CityLine" title="Lufthansa CityLine">Lufthansa CityLine</a> &#8211; German regional airline headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> and part of <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Regional" title="Lufthansa Regional">Lufthansa Regional</a></li>\n<li><a Verona</a> and part of <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Regional" title="Lufthansa Regional">Lufthansa Regional</a></li></ul></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a> &#8211; the flag carrier airline of <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> based at <a href="/wiki/Vienna_International_Airport" title="Vienna International Airport">Vienna International Airport</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Swiss_International_Air_Lines" title="Swiss International Air Lines">Swiss International Air Lines</a> &#8211; the flag carrier airline of <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> based at <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Airport" title="Zurich Airport">Zurich Airport</a>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Edelweiss_Air" title="Edelweiss Air">Edelweiss Air</a> &#8211; Swiss leisure airline subsidiary</li></ul></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a> &#8211; the flag carrier airline of <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> based at <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airport" title="Brussels Airport">Brussels Airport</a><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Eurowings Group (low-cost or hybrid point-to-point airlines)<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> &#8211; German low-cost airline headquartered in <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" Austria</li></ul></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Cargo" title="Lufthansa Cargo">Lufthansa Cargo</a> &#8211; German cargo airline headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="AeroLogic">AeroLogic</a> &#8211; German cargo airline owned by a joint-venture of Lufthansa (50%) and <a href="/wiki/DHL_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="DHL Express">DHL</a> (50%)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/SunExpress" title="SunExpress">SunExpress</a> &#8211; Turkish leisure airline jointly owned by Lufthansa (50%) and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a> (50%)</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Former subsidiaries (years owned)</dt></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/British_Midland_International" title="British Midland International">British Midland International</a> (2009&#8211;2011, stake owned since 1999) &#8211; British airline subsidiary sold to <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a> and merged into <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> in 2012</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Condor_Flugdienst"
