href="/wiki/German_Cargo" title="German Cargo">German Cargo</a> (1977&#8211;1993) &#8211; cargo subsidiary, reorganized into the current <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Cargo" title="Lufthansa Cargo">Lufthansa Cargo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/German_Airways" title="German Airways">Luftfahrtgesellschaft Walter</a> &#8211; German low-cost regional airline integrated into Eurowings in October 2017, sold to Zeitfracht in 2019</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Italia" title="Lufthansa Italia">Lufthansa Italia</a> (2009&#8211;2011) &#8211; Italian airline subsidiary established, sharing IATA, ICAO, and callsigns with the main Lufthansa</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/SunExpress_Deutschland" title="SunExpress Deutschland">SunExpress Deutschland</a> (2011&#8211;2020) &#8211; German subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/SunExpress" title="SunExpress">SunExpress</a><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aerotelegraph.com_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aerotelegraph.com-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_subsidiaries">Other subsidiaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other subsidiaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In addition to the airlines mentioned above, Lufthansa maintains further aviation affiliated subsidiaries:<sup id="cite_ref-2012_report_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012_report-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Global_Load_Control" title="Global Load Control">Global Load Control</a>, a world leader in remote weight and balance services.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/LSG_Sky_Chefs" class="mw-redirect" title="LSG Sky Chefs">LSG Sky Chefs</a>, the world\'s largest airline caterer, which accounts for one-third of the world\'s <a href="/wiki/Airline_meal" title="Airline meal">airline meals</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Consulting" title="Lufthansa Consulting">Lufthansa Consulting</a>, an international aviation consultancy for airlines, airports, and related industries.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_Training" class="mw-redirect" title="Lufthansa Flight Training">Lufthansa Flight Training</a>, a provider of flight crew training services to various airlines and the main training arm for the airline\'s pilots.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Systems" title="Lufthansa Systems">Lufthansa Systems</a>, the largest European aviation IT provider.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Technik" title="Lufthansa Technik">Lufthansa Technik</a>, aircraft maintenance providers.</li>\n<li>Lufthansa City Center International, a network of independent travel agents who are Lufthansa franchisees</li>\n<li>Lufthansa AirPlus Servicekarten GMBH, (AirPlus International) travel payment company via UATP and Mastercard.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brand_history">Brand history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Brand history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D-AIXI_at_MUC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/D-AIXI_at_MUC.jpg/220px-D-AIXI_at_MUC.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/D-AIXI_at_MUC.jpg/330px-D-AIXI_at_MUC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/D-AIXI_at_MUC.jpg/440px-D-AIXI_at_MUC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4087" data-file-height="2725" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D-AIXI_at_MUC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Lufthansa <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350-900" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350-900">Airbus A350-900 XWB</a> painted in the airline\'s latest livery</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-100_(D-AILW)_of_Lufthansa_arrives_at_Birmingham_Airport,_England_27June2019_arp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Airbus_A319-100_%28D-AILW%29_of_Lufthansa_arrives_at_Birmingham_Airport%2C_England_27June2019_arp.jpg/220px-Airbus_A319-100_%28D-AILW%29_of_Lufthansa_arrives_at_Birmingham_Airport%2C_England_27June2019_arp.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Airbus_A319-100_%28D-AILW%29_of_Lufthansa_arrives_at_Birmingham_Airport%2C_England_27June2019_arp.jpg/330px-Airbus_A319-100_%28D-AILW%29_of_Lufthansa_arrives_at_Birmingham_Airport%2C_England_27June2019_arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Airbus_A319-100_%28D-AILW%29_of_Lufthansa_arrives_at_Birmingham_Airport%2C_England_27June2019_arp.jpg/440px-Airbus_A319-100_%28D-AILW%29_of_Lufthansa_arrives_at_Birmingham_Airport%2C_England_27June2019_arp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5550" data-file-height="3556" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-100_(D-AILW)_of_Lufthansa_arrives_at_Birmingham_Airport,_England_27June2019_arp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319-100</a> of Lufthansa in the post-2018 livery. The stylised crane has been kept.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Lufthansa logo, an encircled stylized <a href="/wiki/Crane_(bird)" title="Crane (bird)">crane</a> in flight, was first created in 1918 by Otto Firle. It was part of the livery of the first German airline, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Luft-Reederei" title="Deutsche Luft-Reederei">Deutsche Luft-Reederei</a> (abbreviated DLR), which began air service on 5 February 1919. In 1926, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Luft_Hansa" title="Deutsche Luft Hansa">Deutsche Luft Hansa</a> adopted this symbol, and in 1954, Lufthansa expressed continuity by adopting it and later in 1963 \xe2\x80\x93 a variant thereof as redesigned by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lisovskyi" title="Robert Lisovskyi">Robert Lisovskyi</a>.\n</p><p>The original creator of the name Lufthansa is believed to be F.A. Fischer von Puturzyn. In 1925, he published a book entitled "Luft-Hansa" which examined the options open to aviation policymakers at the time. Luft Hansa was the name given to the new airline, which resulted from the merger of <a href="/wiki/Junkers" title="Junkers">Junkers</a>\' airline (<a href="/wiki/Junkers_Luftverkehr" class="mw-redirect" title="Junkers Luftverkehr">Luftverkehr AG</a>) and <i>Deutscher Aero Lloyd</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-lh_chronicle_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lh_chronicle-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After World War II, the company kept blue and yellow as its main colours and the crane logo. Since the beginning of the 1960s, <a href="/wiki/Helvetica" title="Helvetica">Helvetica</a> was used for the company name in the livery. The 1970s retro livery featured the top half of the fuselage painted in all-white on top and the lower fuselage (bottom half, including the engines) was gray/silver aluminium, below a blue cheatline window band and a black painted nose. The crane logo was painted blue on the engines, on the bottom half of the fuselage just below the cockpit windows, and a yellow circle inside a blue band on the tail.\n</p><p>German designer <a href="/wiki/Otl_Aicher" title="Otl Aicher">Otl Aicher</a> created a comprehensive corporate design for the airline in 1967. The crane logo was now always displayed in a circle which, on the livery, was yellow on an otherwise blue tailfin. Helvetica was used as the main typeface for both the livery and publications. The blue band and general paint scheme of the aircraft were retained from the previous livery.\n</p><p>Aicher\'s concept was retained in the 1988 design. The window band was removed and the fuselage was painted in grey.\n</p><p>In 2018, Lufthansa refreshed their livery. The encircled crane was retained, however, the background was changed from yellow to dark blue. The vertical stabilizer and the rear fuselage was all painted in dark blue, with the tail cone remained white. The main fuselage was painted in all white, and the brand name "Lufthansa" was painted above the windows, also in dark blue.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alliances_and_partnerships">Alliances and partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Alliances and partnerships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FRA_LH_Lounge_First_seating.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/FRA_LH_Lounge_First_seating.jpg/220px-FRA_LH_Lounge_First_seating.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/FRA_LH_Lounge_First_seating.jpg/330px-FRA_LH_Lounge_First_seating.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/FRA_LH_Lounge_First_seating.jpg/440px-FRA_LH_Lounge_First_seating.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FRA_LH_Lounge_First_seating.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Lufthansa First Class lounge at <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a></div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial">Commercial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Commercial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Lufthansa bought a 19% stake in <a href="/wiki/JetBlue_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="JetBlue Airways">JetBlue Airways</a> in December 2007 and entered a code-sharing agreement with the airline. It was the first major investment by a European carrier in an American carrier since the <a href="/wiki/EU%E2%80%93U.S._Open_Skies_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="EU\xe2\x80\x93U.S. Open Skies Agreement">EU\xe2\x80\x93U.S. Open Skies Agreement</a> came into effect in 2008. Lufthansa sold its stake in JetBlue in March 2015.\n</p><p>In late 2007, Lufthansa Cargo was forced to relocate a hub from <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> to <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>.\n</p><p>On 28 August 2008, Lufthansa and <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a> announced that they were negotiating joining together.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lufthansa acquired a 45% stake in Brussels Airlines in 2009. It has an option to acquire the remaining 55% by 2017. As a part of the deal Brussels Airlines joined <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> in December 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 October 2008, Lufthansa exercised its option to purchase a further 60% share in <a href="/wiki/British_Midland_International" title="British Midland International">BMI</a> (in addition to the 20% Lufthansa already owned), this resulted in a dispute with the former owner <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bishop,_Baron_Glendonbrook" title="Michael Bishop, Baron Glendonbrook">Sir Michael Bishop</a>. Both parties reached an agreement at the end of June 2009, and the acquisition took place with effect from 1 July 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Lufthansa acquired the remaining 20% from Scandinavian Airlines on 1 November 2009, taking complete control of BMI.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lufthansa completed the purchase of <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a> from the Austrian government in January 2009.\n</p><p>In 2010, Lufthansa was named in a <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> investigation into price-fixing, but was not fined because it acted as a whistleblower.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2012, Lufthansa completed the sale of BMI to <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a> (IAG), owner of British Airways and Iberia for \xc2\xa3172.5 million.\n</p><p>In July 2012, a Qantas\xe2\x80\x93Lufthansa Technik maintenance deal for Tullamarine airport fell through due to having insufficient engine maintenance work to support the partnership. This resulted in 164 engineers being made redundant. This followed just months after the closing of heavy maintenance operations, which resulted in 400 additional job losses. It was announced that the Lufthansa Technik\xe2\x80\x93Qantas partnership would end in September.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lufthansa also coordinates scheduling and ticket sales on transatlantic flights with Air Canada and United Airlines (as do Brussels Airlines, Swiss and Austrian Airlines). Lufthansa (with Swiss and Austrian Airlines) cooperates similarly with ANA on flights to Japan. Both ventures required the approval of competition authorities.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Until April 2009 Lufthansa inventory and departure control systems, based on <a href="/wiki/Unisys" title="Unisys">Unisys</a> were managed by <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Systems" title="Lufthansa Systems">LH Systems</a>. Lufthansa reservations systems were outsourced to Amadeus in the early 1990s. Following a decision to outsource all components of the <a href="/wiki/Passenger_Service_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Passenger Service System">Passenger Service System</a>, the functions were outsourced to the Alt\xc3\xa9a platform managed by <a href="/wiki/Amadeus_IT_Group" title="Amadeus IT Group">Amadeus</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Partner_airlines">Partner airlines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Partner airlines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Lufthansa describes <a href="/wiki/Air_Malta" title="Air Malta">Air Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxair" title="Luxair">Luxair</a>, and <a href="/wiki/LATAM" class="mw-redirect" title="LATAM">LATAM</a>  as partner airlines. The partnerships mainly involve code-sharing and recognition of each other\'s frequent flier programmes.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorships">Sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sponsorships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Lufthansa sponsors <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> club <a href="/wiki/Eintracht_Frankfurt" title="Eintracht Frankfurt">Eintracht Frankfurt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The Lufthansa Group also sponsors the German Sports Aid Foundation - promoting its sociopolitical goals and the athletes it sponsors.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">Destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lufthansa_destinations" title="List of Lufthansa destinations">List of Lufthansa destinations</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Codeshare_agreements">Codeshare agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Codeshare agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lufthansa <a href="/wiki/Codeshare_agreement" title="Codeshare agreement">codeshares</a> with the following airlines:<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 15em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Air_Astana" title="Air Astana">Air Astana</a><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/AirBaltic" title="AirBaltic">airBaltic</a><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Air_China" title="Air China">Air China</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Air_Dolomiti" title="Air Dolomiti">Air Dolomiti</a> <sup>LH</sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Air_India" title="Air India">Air India</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Air_Malta" title="Air Malta">Air Malta</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Air_New_Zealand" title="Air New Zealand">Air New Zealand</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/All_Nippon_Airways" title="All Nippon Airways">All Nippon Airways</a><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Asiana_Airlines" title="Asiana Airlines">Asiana Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a> <sup>LH</sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Avianca" title="Avianca">Avianca</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a> <sup>LH</sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines" title="Copa Airlines">Copa Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Croatia_Airlines" title="Croatia Airlines">Croatia Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/EgyptAir" class="mw-redirect" title="EgyptAir">EgyptAir</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Airlines" title="Ethiopian Airlines">Ethiopian Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> <sup>LH</sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/LATAM_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="LATAM Airlines">LATAM Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Luxair" title="Luxair">Luxair</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Shenzhen_Airlines" title="Shenzhen Airlines">Shenzhen Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/South_African_Airways" title="South African Airways">South African Airways</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/SunExpress" title="SunExpress">SunExpress</a> <sup>LH</sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Swiss_International_Air_Lines" title="Swiss International Air Lines">Swiss International Air Lines</a> <sup>LH</sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/TAP_Air_Portugal" title="TAP Air Portugal">TAP Air Portugal</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thai_Airways" title="Thai Airways">Thai Airways</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Vistara" title="Vistara">Vistara</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<p><sup>LH</sup> Part of the Lufthansa Group.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet">Fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_fleet" title="Lufthansa fleet">Lufthansa fleet</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft_naming_conventions">Aircraft naming conventions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Aircraft naming conventions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In September 1960, a Lufthansa Boeing 707 (D-ABOC), which would serve the Frankfurt-New York intercontinental route, was christened <i>Berlin</i> after the divided city of Berlin by then-mayor <a href="/wiki/Willy_Brandt" title="Willy Brandt">Willy Brandt</a>. Following <i>Berlin</i>, other Lufthansa 707 planes were named "<a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">M\xc3\xbcnchen</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>." With these names, the company established a tradition of <a href="/wiki/Ship_naming_and_launching" class="mw-redirect" title="Ship naming and launching">naming</a> the planes in its fleet after German cities and towns or federal states, with a rule of thumb that the airplane make, size, or route would correspond roughly to the relative size or importance of the city or town it was named after.\n</p><p>This tradition continued, with two notable exceptions, until 2010: The first was an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-300">Airbus A340-300</a> registered D-AIFC, named "Gander/Halifax", after <a href="/wiki/Gander,_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Gander, Newfoundland and Labrador">Gander</a> and <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Halifax Regional Municipality">Halifax</a>, two Canadian cities along the standard flight path from Europe to North America. It became the first Lufthansa airplane named after a non-German city. The name commemorates the hospitality of the communities of Gander and Halifax, which served as improvised safe havens for the passengers and crew of the multitude of international aircraft unable to return to their originating airports during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Yellow_Ribbon" title="Operation Yellow Ribbon">Operation Yellow Ribbon</a> after the <a href="/wiki/September_11,_2001_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="September 11, 2001 attacks">September 11, 2001 attacks</a>. The other aircraft not named after a German city was an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321-100" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A321-100">Airbus A321-100</a> registered as D-AIRA, which was designated <i>Finkenwerder</i> in honor of the Airbus facility in the district of <a href="/wiki/Finkenwerder" title="Finkenwerder">Hamburg-Finkenwerder</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-lhtaufnamen2_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lhtaufnamen2-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> where about 40% of Airbus narrowbody models are manufactured.\n</p><p>In February 2010, Lufthansa announced that its first two <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380s</a> would be named <i>Frankfurt am Main</i> (D-AIMA) and <i>M\xc3\xbcnchen</i> (D-AIMB) after Lufthansa\'s two hub airports. Subsequent A380 aircraft were named after other Lufthansa Group hub airports <i><a href="/wiki/Zurich" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich">Zurich</a></i>, <i>Wien</i> (<a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>) and <i>Br\xc3\xbcssel</i> (<a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>) and the major German cities of <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a></i>. The remaining A380s were named after <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> hub cities <i>Tokyo</i>, <i>Beijing</i>, <i>Johannesburg</i>, <i>New York</i>, <i>San Francisco</i> and <i>Delhi</i>. However, D-AIMN <i>San Francisco</i> was renamed <i>Deutschland</i> (Germany) in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-lhtaufnamen2_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lhtaufnamen2-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 2016, there are several short- and long-haul aircraft in Lufthansa\'s fleet that do not bear any name. They either never received one or their former one has been given to a newer aircraft, which was the case for several <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400s</a>. For example, the former <i>Bayern</i> (<a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>), a Boeing 747-400 still in active service lost that name to a new <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-8" title="Boeing 747-8">Boeing 747-8I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lhtaufnamen2_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lhtaufnamen2-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vintage_aircraft_restoration">Vintage aircraft restoration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Vintage aircraft restoration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Technik" title="Lufthansa Technik">Lufthansa Technik</a>, the airline\'s maintenance arm, restored a <a href="/wiki/Junkers_Ju_52/3m" class="mw-redirect" title="Junkers Ju 52/3m">Junkers Ju 52/3m</a> built in 1936 to <a href="/wiki/Airworthy" class="mw-redirect" title="Airworthy">airworthiness</a>; this aircraft was in use on the 10-hour Berlin to Rome route, across the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>, in the 1930s. Lufthansa is now restoring a <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Super_Constellation" class="mw-redirect" title="Lockheed Super Constellation">Lockheed Super Constellation</a>, using parts from three such aircraft bought at auctions. Lufthansa\'s Super Constellations and L1649 "Starliners" served routes such as <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>-<a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>-<a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">Dakar</a>-<a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">Caracas</a>-<a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Chile" class="mw-redirect" title="Santiago, Chile">Santiago</a>. Lufthansa Technik recruits retired employees and volunteers for skilled labour.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airbus_A380">Airbus A380</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Airbus A380">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lufthansa had initially ordered a total of 15 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A380-800">Airbus A380-800</a>, of which by June 2012 ten were delivered. In September 2011, the order was increased by two more to 17, this order was confirmed on 14 March 2013. However, in September 2013 it was announced that the Lufthansa Supervisory Board had approved the purchase of only twelve of the first 15 A380s. Thus, a total of 14 A380s have been added to the fleet.\n</p><p>Lufthansa uses its A380s from and to Frankfurt am Main (9 aircraft) and since March 2018 to and from Munich as well (5 aircraft). From 6 to 12 December 2011, Lufthansa already used an A380 once a day on the route from Munich to New York-JFK. This happened mainly against the backdrop of Christmas shopping in New York City.\n</p><p>On 13 March 2019, Lufthansa announced that it will be removing 6 <a href="/wiki/A380" class="mw-redirect" title="A380">A380</a> aircraft from the fleet and replacing them with Boeing 787-9 and Airbus A350-900 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 8 March 2020, Lufthansa announced that it would be grounding all of its A380 aircraft due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frequent-flyer_programme">Frequent-flyer programme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Frequent-flyer programme">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Miles_%26_More" title="Miles &amp; More">Miles &amp; More</a></div>\n<p>Lufthansa\'s <a href="/wiki/Frequent-flyer_program" title="Frequent-flyer program">frequent-flyer</a> programme is called <i>Miles &amp; More</i>, and is shared among several European airlines, including all of Lufthansa\'s subsidiary airlines (excluding the <a href="/wiki/SunExpress" title="SunExpress">SunExpress</a> joint ventures), plus <a href="/wiki/Adria_Airways" title="Adria Airways">Adria Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Condor_Flugdienst" class="mw-redirect" title="Condor Flugdienst">Condor Flugdienst</a> (formerly owned by Lufthansa), <a href="/wiki/Croatia_Airlines" title="Croatia Airlines">Croatia Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Luxair" title="Luxair">Luxair</a> (stake formerly held by Lufthansa).<sup id="cite_ref-Miles_&amp;_More_partners_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miles_&amp;_More_partners-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Miles &amp; More members may earn miles on Lufthansa flights and <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> partner flights, as well as through Lufthansa credit cards, and purchases made through the Lufthansa shops. Status within Miles &amp; More is determined by miles flown during one calendar year with specific partners. Membership levels include: Miles &amp; More member (no minimal threshold), Frequent Traveller (Silver, 35,000-mile (56,000&#160;km) threshold or 30 individual flights), Senator (Gold, 100,000-mile (160,000&#160;km) threshold), and HON Circle (Black, 600,000-mile (970,000&#160;km) threshold over two calendar years). All Miles &amp; More status levels higher than Miles &amp; More member offer lounge access and executive bonus miles, with the higher levels offering more exclusive benefits.<sup id="cite_ref-Miles_&amp;_More_status_levels_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miles_&amp;_More_status_levels-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cabins">Cabins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Cabins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Class">First Class</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: First Class">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747-830,_Lufthansa_AN2119979.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119979.jpg/220px-Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119979.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119979.jpg/330px-Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119979.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119979.jpg/440px-Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119979.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747-830,_Lufthansa_AN2119979.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/First_class_(aviation)" title="First class (aviation)">First Class</a> on board one of Lufthansa\'s Boeing 747-8Is in a 1-2-1 layout.</div></div></div>\n<p>First Class is offered on most long-haul aircraft (all A340-600s, the front part of the upper deck of all Airbus A380s, and the main deck nose section of all Boeing 747-8Is). Each seat converts to a 2 metres (6&#160;ft 7&#160;in) bed, includes laptop power outlets, as well as entertainment facilities. Meals are available on demand. Lufthansa offers dedicated First Class check-in counters at most airports, and offers dedicated First Class lounges in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, as well as a dedicated first-class terminal in Frankfurt. Arriving passengers have the option of using Lufthansa\'s First Class arrival facilities, as well as the new Welcome Lounge. Lufthansa has introduced a new First Class product aboard the Airbus A380 and plans to gradually introduce it on all of its long-haul aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\nWith the new program SCORE, introduced to boost profits by 1.5 billion euros over the following years, LH will stop route expansion and extensively decrease its First Class offerings on most routes.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> However, First Class will not be completely eliminated, as the company plans to introduce a new First Class cabin on the Boeing 777-9, with a primary focus on privacy.  However, the new first class will not be on the first few 777-9s, since those will not have any first class cabin.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_Class">Business Class</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Business Class">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747-830,_Lufthansa_AN2119980.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119980.jpg/220px-Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119980.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119980.jpg/330px-Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119980.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119980.jpg/440px-Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2119980.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747-830,_Lufthansa_AN2119980.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Business Class in a 2-2 layout on the upper deck of a Boeing 747-8I. Business Class on all of the airline\'s other wide-body aircraft has a 2-2-2 layout.</div></div></div>\n<p>Business Class is offered on all long-haul aircraft. Seats convert to 2 metres (6&#160;ft 7&#160;in) lie-flat beds and include laptop power outlets and entertainment facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-CNT_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNT-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Lufthansa offers dedicated Business Class check-in counters at all airports, as well as dedicated Business Class lounges at most airports, or contract lounges at other airports, as well as the Lufthansa Welcome Lounge upon arrival in Frankfurt. As of 2014, Business Class on all wide-body aircraft feature lie-flat seats.<sup id="cite_ref-Business_Traveler_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Business_Traveler-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Lufthansa released plans for a new business class set to be released in 2022 on either the Boeing 787-9 or Airbus A350-900, and will retrofit the rest of the fleet in the coming years.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Premium_Economy_Class">Premium Economy Class</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Premium Economy Class">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Introduced in 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Lufthansa\'s long-haul Premium Economy is being rolled out on all long-haul aircraft, starting with some Boeing 747-8Is. Similar in design to <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a>\'s Premium Economy or <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>\' World Traveller Plus cabins, Premium Economy features 38-inch (970&#160;mm) pitch along with up to 3 inches (76&#160;mm) more width than economy class, depending on the aircraft. The seats also feature a 11 or 12 inches (280 or 300&#160;mm) personal seat-back entertainment screen and a larger armrest separating seats. Along with the planned introduction of the Boeing 777-9X, the airline plans to add a new Premium Economy cabin with a "shell" design. These seats are also to be installed on SWISS\' Boeing 777-300ERs and Airbus A340-300s from the first and second quarter of 2021, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_Class">Economy Class</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Economy Class">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747-830,_Lufthansa_AN2100134.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2100134.jpg/220px-Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2100134.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2100134.jpg/330px-Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2100134.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2100134.jpg/440px-Boeing_747-830%2C_Lufthansa_AN2100134.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747-830,_Lufthansa_AN2100134.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Economy Class on a 747-8I in a 3-4-3 layout.</div></div></div>\n<p>Lufthansa\'s long-haul Economy Class is offered on all long-haul aircraft. All have a 31-inch (790&#160;mm) seat pitch except the Airbus A380s, which have a 33-inch (840&#160;mm) seat pitch. Passengers receive meals, as well as free drinks. The whole fleet offers Audio-Video-On-Demand (<a href="/wiki/AVOD" class="mw-redirect" title="AVOD">AVOD</a>) screens in Economy Class.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_lounges_and_terminals">Airport lounges and terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Airport lounges and terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Flughafen,_Lufthansa_First_Class_Terminal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Lufthansa_First_Class_Terminal.jpg/220px-Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Lufthansa_First_Class_Terminal.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Lufthansa_First_Class_Terminal.jpg/330px-Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Lufthansa_First_Class_Terminal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Lufthansa_First_Class_Terminal.jpg/440px-Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Lufthansa_First_Class_Terminal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1288" data-file-height="966" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Flughafen,_Lufthansa_First_Class_Terminal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i>First Class Terminal</i> at <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Lufthansa operates four types of lounges within its destination network: First Class, Senator, Business, and Welcome Lounges. Each departure lounge is accessible both through travel class, or Miles and More/Star Alliance status; the Welcome Lounge is limited to arriving premium passengers of the Lufthansa Group and United Airlines only.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Lufthansa also operates a dedicated first class terminal at Frankfurt Airport. The first terminal of its kind, access is limited only to departing Lufthansa First Class, same day Lufthansa Group first class and HON Circle members. Approximately 200 staff care for approximately 300 passengers per day in the terminal, which features a full-service restaurant, full bar, cigar lounge, relaxation rooms, and offices, as well as bath facilities. Guests are driven directly to their departing flight by <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_S-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz S-Class">Mercedes-Benz S-Class</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porsche_Cayenne" title="Porsche Cayenne">Porsche Cayenne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porsche_Panamera" title="Porsche Panamera">Porsche Panamera</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_V-Class" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercedes-Benz V-Class">Mercedes-Benz V-Class</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_service">Bus service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Bus service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lufthansa previously operated a check-in point in the city limits of <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a> and a bus service from Nuremberg to <a href="/wiki/Munich_Airport" title="Munich Airport">Munich Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>This is a list of accidents and incidents involving Lufthansa mainline aircraft since 1956. For earlier occurrences, refer to <a href="/wiki/Hestnutan_Accident" class="mw-redirect" title="Hestnutan Accident">Deutsche Luft Hansa</a>. For accidents and incidents on Lufthansa-branded flights which were operated by other airlines, see the respective articles (<a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_CityLine#Accidents_and_incidents" title="Lufthansa CityLine">Lufthansa CityLine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Cargo#Accidents_and_incidents" title="Lufthansa Cargo">Lufthansa Cargo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_288" class="mw-redirect" title="Lufthansa Flight 288">Contact Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germanwings#Incidents_and_accidents" title="Germanwings">Germanwings</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Air_Dolomiti#Accidents_and_incidents" title="Air Dolomiti">Air Dolomiti</a>).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fatal">Fatal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Fatal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>On 11 January 1959, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_502" title="Lufthansa Flight 502">Lufthansa Flight 502</a>, a Lufthansa <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Super_Constellation" class="mw-redirect" title="Lockheed Super Constellation">Lockheed Super Constellation</a> (<a href="/wiki/Aircraft_registration" title="Aircraft registration">registered</a> D-ALAK) crashed onto a beach shortly off <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro-Gale%C3%A3o_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio de Janeiro-Gale\xc3\xa3o International Airport">Gale\xc3\xa3o Airport</a> in Rio de Janeiro following a scheduled passenger flight from <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, Germany. Of the 29 passengers and 10 crew members on board, only the co-pilot and 2 flight attendants survived. The investigation into the accident resulted in blaming the pilots for having executed a too low approach, which may have been caused by fatigue.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 4 December 1961, a Lufthansa <a href="/wiki/Boeing_720" title="Boeing 720">Boeing 720</a> (registered D-ABOK) crashed of unknown causes near <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a> during a training flight from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, killing the three occupants. It was the first crash involving an aircraft of that type.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 15 July 1964, another Boeing 720 (registered D-ABOP) crashed during a training flight, with the three people, including <a href="/wiki/Werner_Baake" title="Werner Baake">Werner Baake</a>, on board losing their lives (in what was only the second crash for this aircraft type). The accident occurred near <a href="/wiki/Ansbach" title="Ansbach">Ansbach</a> after the pilots had lost control of the aircraft when executing an <a href="/wiki/Aileron_roll" title="Aileron roll">aileron roll</a>.</li>\n<li>On 28 January 1966 at 17:50 local time, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_005" title="Lufthansa Flight 005">Lufthansa Flight 5</a> from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> to <a href="/wiki/Bremen" title="Bremen">Bremen</a>, which was operated using a <a href="/wiki/Convair_CV-240_family" title="Convair CV-240 family">Convair CV-440 Metropolitan</a> registered D-ACAT, crashed 0.5 kilometres (0.31&#160;mi) short of <a href="/wiki/Bremen_Airport" title="Bremen Airport">Bremen Airport</a>, killing all 42 passengers and 4 crew members on board. The pilots had tried to execute a <a href="/wiki/Go-around" title="Go-around">go-around</a> when approaching the airport, during which the aircraft <a href="/wiki/Stall_(flight)" class="mw-redirect" title="Stall (flight)">stalled</a> and went out of control, possibly due to pilot error.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:19700712_LH_Jumbo_GFAu46kl15.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/19700712_LH_Jumbo_GFAu46kl15.jpg/220px-19700712_LH_Jumbo_GFAu46kl15.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/19700712_LH_Jumbo_GFAu46kl15.jpg/330px-19700712_LH_Jumbo_GFAu46kl15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/19700712_LH_Jumbo_GFAu46kl15.jpg/440px-19700712_LH_Jumbo_GFAu46kl15.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:19700712_LH_Jumbo_GFAu46kl15.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>D-ABYB, the aircraft destroyed in the Flight 540 accident, was the 2nd of 3 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-100" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-100">Boeing 747-100s</a> delivered to Lufthansa.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> It is seen here during a promotional event at <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Airport" title="Nuremberg Airport">Nuremberg Airport</a> in 1970.</div></div></div>\n<ul><li>On 20 November 1974 at 07:54 local time, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_540" title="Lufthansa Flight 540">Lufthansa Flight 540</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747-100</a> (registered D-ABYB), lost power and crashed shortly after take-off at <a href="/wiki/Jomo_Kenyatta_International_Airport" title="Jomo Kenyatta International Airport">Jomo Kenyatta International Airport</a> in what was the first air accident involving a Boeing 747. 55 out of the 140 passengers and 4 out of the 17 crew lost their lives, making it the worst accident in the history of the airline.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 26 July 1979 at 21:32 <a href="/wiki/Universal_Time_Coordinated" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Time Coordinated">UTC</a>, a cargo-configured <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">Boeing 707</a> (registered D-ABUY) that was en route <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_527" title="Lufthansa Flight 527">Lufthansa Flight 527</a> from <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> to <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">Dakar</a> and onwards to Germany crashed into a mountain 25 kilometres (16&#160;mi) from <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro-Gale%C3%A3o_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio de Janeiro-Gale\xc3\xa3o International Airport">Gale\xc3\xa3o Airport</a> during initial climb, killing the three crew members on board. A flawed communication between the pilots and the air traffic controller had resulted in the aircraft flying on a wrong path.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 14 September 1993, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_2904" title="Lufthansa Flight 2904">Lufthansa Flight 2904</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320-200</a> (registered D-AIPN) flying from Frankfurt to <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> with 64 passengers and 4 crew members on board, overran the runway upon landing at <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Chopin_Airport" title="Warsaw Chopin Airport">Warsaw-Okecie Airport</a>, and crashed into an earth embankment, resulting in the death of the <a href="/wiki/Co-pilot" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-pilot">co-pilot</a> and one passenger.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-fatal">Non-fatal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Non-fatal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>On 20 December 1973 at 00:33 local time, a Lufthansa <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">Boeing 707</a> (registered D-ABOT) with 98 passengers and 11 crew members on board collided with a <a href="/wiki/Marker_beacon" title="Marker beacon">middle marker</a> shack upon approaching <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_International_Airport" title="Indira Gandhi International Airport">Palam Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a> following a scheduled passenger flight from <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a> (as part of a multi-leg flight back to Germany). There were no injuries, but the aircraft was damaged beyond repair. Visibility was poor at the time of the accident.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 18 October 1983, a Boeing 747-200 freighter ran off the runway at Kai Tak airport in Hong Kong and got bogged in the grass after an engine failure during take-off.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 11 June 2018, one of the airline\'s Airbus A340-300s, registered as D-AIFA, was being towed to its departure gate at Frankfurt Airport when the towing vehicle caught fire. Despite the quick action of the airport fire brigade, the aircraft suffered substantial fire and smoke damage to the nose and flight deck. Six people were treated for smoke inhalation.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hijackings">Hijackings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Hijackings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>In 1972, the year of the <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">Munich Summer Olympics</a>, there were four reported hijackings involving Lufthansa aircraft:\n<ul><li>On 22 February, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_649" title="Lufthansa Flight 649">Flight 649</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-200">Boeing 747-200</a> (registered D-ABYD) with 172 passengers and 15 crew members on board was hijacked en route from <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a> to <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> (as part of a multi-leg flight from <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>) by five <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian people">Palestinian</a> terrorists who thus wanted to press a $5 million ransom from the German government. The aircraft landed at <a href="/wiki/Aden_International_Airport" title="Aden International Airport">Aden International Airport</a>, and the hostages were released on the following day once the demands of the perpetrators were accepted.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 10 July, a similar hijacking attempt occurred on board a Lufthansa <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-100" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-100">Boeing 737-100</a> during a flight from <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> to <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (October 2013)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li>11 October a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing 727</a> was hijacked on a flight from <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>. Upon landing at <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>, the perpetrator tried to flee but was captured by police forces.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (October 2013)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li>On 29 October, two men hijacked <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_615" title="Lufthansa Flight 615">Flight 615</a> with 11 other passengers and 7 crew members on board during a flight from <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ankara" title="Ankara">Ankara</a> (and onwards to Germany), in order to liberate the three surviving members of the <a href="/wiki/Black_September_(group)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black September (group)">Black September</a> group responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Munich_massacre" title="Munich massacre">Munich massacre</a>. Whilst the hijacked <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing 727</a> (registered D-ABIG) was forced to circle over <a href="/wiki/Zagreb_Airport" title="Zagreb Airport">Zagreb Airport</a> in danger of eventual <a href="/wiki/Fuel_starvation" title="Fuel starvation">fuel starvation</a>, the West German authorities decided to comply with the demands. The prisoners were handed over and the aircraft was allowed to be flown to <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a>, where the hostages were released.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-google8_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google8-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-faz_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faz-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li>On 17 December 1973, in the wake of the events surrounding <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Flight_110" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan Am Flight 110">Pan Am Flight 110</a>, a parked Lufthansa <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737-100</a> (registered D-ABEY) was hijacked at <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci-Fiumicino_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Leonardo da Vinci-Fiumicino Airport">Leonardo da Vinci-Fiumicino Airport</a> in Rome. 10 Italian hostages that had been taken by <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestinian</a> terrorists at the airport were forced into the aircraft by 5 perpetrators, and the German crew (2 pilots and 2 flight attendants) that was on board preparing the departure to <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> had to fly the aircraft instead first to <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> and then to several other airports until the ordeal ended at <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_International_Airport" title="Kuwait International Airport">Kuwait International Airport</a> the next day, where the hijackers surrendered.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 28 June 1977, a Lufthansa <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing 727</a> was hijacked during a flight from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> to <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> and forced to divert to <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (October 2013)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_181" title="Lufthansa Flight 181">Hijacking of the Landshut</a> occurred on 13 October 1977, at a time when West Germany had come under intense terroristic pressure known as <a href="/wiki/German_Autumn" title="German Autumn">German Autumn</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737-200</a> (registered D-ABCE) was hijacked en route Flight 181 from <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca" title="Palma de Mallorca">Palma de Mallorca</a> to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> by 4 terrorists of the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_Palestine" title="Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine">Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine</a>, who thus wanted to force the German government to release several <a href="/wiki/Red_Army_Faction" title="Red Army Faction">RAF</a> terrorists. The crew had to divert the aircraft with 87 other passengers first to Rome, and then onwards to <a href="/wiki/Larnaca" title="Larnaca">Larnaca</a>, Bahrain, <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aden" title="Aden">Aden</a> (where the captain was killed when he returned to the aircraft after negotiations with the local authorities), and finally to <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a> in an ordeal that took several days. At <a href="/wiki/Aden_Adde_International_Airport" title="Aden Adde International Airport">Mogadishu Airport</a>, the German <a href="/wiki/GSG_9" title="GSG 9">GSG 9</a> special forces stormed the aircraft in the early hours of 18 October local time, killing 3 terrorists and freeing all hostages.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 12 September 1979, a hijacking attempt occurred on board a Lufthansa Boeing 727 on a flight from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, but the perpetrator quickly surrendered.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (October 2013)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li>Three hijackings occurred in due course in early 1985:\n<ul><li>On 27 February, a Boeing 727 was hijacked en route a Lufthansa flight from Frankfurt to <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a>. Two perpetrators forced the pilots to divert the aircraft (with 35 other passengers on board) to <a href="/wiki/Vienna_International_Airport" title="Vienna International Airport">Vienna International Airport</a>, where they surrendered.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (October 2013)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li>On 27 March, another 727 was hijacked, this time on a flight from Munich to <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>. A man demanded the pilots to divert to <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>. During a fuel stop at <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, the aircraft was stormed and the perpetrator arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (October 2013)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li>Only two days later, a mentally ill person onboard a Lufthansa <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737-200</a> on a flight from <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> to London demanded to be taken to Hawaii instead.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (October 2013)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul></li>\n<li>On 11 February 1993, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Flight_592" title="Lufthansa Flight 592">Lufthansa Flight 592</a> from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> to <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a> via <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a> with 94 passengers and 10 crew members was hijacked during the first leg by 20-year-old Nebiu Zewolde Demeke, who forced the pilots to divert the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A310" title="Airbus A310">Airbus A310</a> (registered D-AIDM) to the United States, with the intent of securing the <a href="/wiki/Right_of_asylum" title="Right of asylum">right of asylum</a> there. Demeke, who had been on the flight to be <a href="/wiki/Deportation" title="Deportation">deported</a> back to his native <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, surrendered to authorities upon arrival at <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a> in New York City. No passengers or crew members were harmed during the 12-hour ordeal.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment_relations">Employment relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Employment relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Relations between Lufthansa and their pilots have been very tense in the past years, with many strikes occurring, causing many flights to be cancelled, as well as major losses to the company.<sup id="cite_ref-ksb/bk_2015_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ksb/bk_2015-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> A major dispute between Lufthansa and the pilot\'s union has been settled after nearly five years and overall 14 strikes in December 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germanwings_crisis_management">Germanwings crisis management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Germanwings crisis management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Germanwings_Flight_9525" title="Germanwings Flight 9525">Germanwings Flight 9525</a></div>\n<p>Germanwings was a subsidiary of Lufthansa. Carsten Spohr, Lufthansa\'s CEO, oversaw the <a href="/wiki/Germanwings_Flight_9525" title="Germanwings Flight 9525">Germanwings Flight 9525</a> accident, "the darkest day for Lufthansa in its 60-year history".<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nonetheless, damage control by Spohr and his team was poor according to several sources, as compared to other CEOs in the face of a major accident, with contradictory information given about the mental health and the airworthiness of the co-pilot Andreas Lubitz. It was revealed that Lubitz suffered from a severe case of depression and mental disorders and had intentionally crashed Germanwings Flight 9525 into the French Alps, killing all 150 aboard. Spohr had misleadingly said the co-pilot "was 100% airworthy without any restrictions, without any conditions".<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GDS_surcharge">GDS surcharge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: GDS surcharge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 1 September 2015, Lufthansa implemented a 16 euro surcharge on <a href="/wiki/Global_Distribution_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Distribution System">Global Distribution System</a> bookings. The surcharge is payable unless tickets are purchased directly from the airline\'s website, or at its service centres and ticket counters at the airport. In a statement responding to Lufthansa\'s strategy, Amadeus, a travel technology company, said the new model would make "comparison and transparency more difficult because travellers will now be forced to go to multiple channels to search for the best fares.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> For the period between 1\xe2\x80\x9314 September, the airline experienced a 16.1% drop in revenue, indicating to some that the new fee backfired, although the airline maintains the statement that the decrease was due to the pilot strike, and "other seasonal effects".<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deportation_flights">Deportation flights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Deportation flights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Activists from Germany have criticised Lufthansa for performing deportation flights on behalf of the German government.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> In 2019, 4,573 people were deported on their planes, while their subsidiary Eurowings performed 1,312 deportations.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> This totals more than 25% of deportations in Germany in 2019. At least two deportees perished during transport.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Treatment_of_World_War_II-era_past">Treatment of World War II-era past</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Treatment of World War II-era past">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lufthansa has been criticized for lack of transparency about the use of more than 10,000 forced laborers, many of them children, by its predecessor company, Deutsche Luft Hansa, during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Germany#Air_transport" title="Transport in Germany">Air transport in Germany</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_airlines_of_Germany" title="List of airlines of Germany">List of airlines of Germany</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The company that today is known as <i>Deutsche Lufthansa AG</i> was founded as <i>Aktiengesellschaft f\xc3\xbcr Luftverkehrsbedarf (Luftag)</i> on 6 January 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-fi54_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fi54-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> It sees itself in the tradition of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Luft_Hansa" title="Deutsche Luft Hansa">Deutsche Lufthansa</a>, the former German national airline that was founded in 1926 and liquidated in 1951, whose name and logo it acquired in 1954.<sup id="cite_ref-lex_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lex-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Lufthansa frequently names "1926" as its founding date, but it is not the legal successor of the earlier airline.<sup id="cite_ref-DLHhistory_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DLHhistory-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Lufthansa also counts <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vienna_International_Airport" title="Vienna International Airport">Vienna International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Airport" title="Zurich Airport">Zurich Airport</a> as its hubs.<sup id="cite_ref-LHhubs_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LHhubs-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> They are not listed here because they are home to Lufthansa\'s subsidiaries <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swiss_International_Air_Lines" title="Swiss International Air Lines">Swiss International Air Lines</a>, respectively. For the same reason, all other <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> bases are omitted.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Citations">Citations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lufthansa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section:
